<Author>cpmgrp
<Content>Sterile, snooty, outrageously expensive. Sterile, snooty, outrageously expensive. Rooms ok, the usual Hilton experience only with a French attitude. Which is why I still have to give it above average. The kids in the business center were terrific. No view to speak of. $30 for continental, $45 for full breakfast. $9 for a half cup of caf au lait. I found a private car shuttle for $47, just Google it a day in advance and make a reservation. The Ryan Air folks let me slide on my luggage weight coming out of Lubeck, but nailed me good out of France.An observation about TripAdvisor (if youe seen this in other of my posts, feel free to skip): I used it extensively when planning a last-minute 3-week trip to Europe, was very happy to have the service and felt I should pay back with my comments. I think you have to read between the lines and determine the type of traveler writing the review compared to your own type. Ie stayed in places that were highly recommended and turned out to be terrible; and the reverse. Try to judge whether the contributor is complaining about a one-time, bad experience as a result of an inattentive employee as opposed to a basic fault with the property itself. If a restaurant manager was rude, so what. If the place floods, and smells -- that a different story.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great vacation We were at the Hilton Arc de Triomphe from May 10-17th 2006. We are in in our early 30's and were celebrating our anniversary, my birthday and valentines all in one! We had not had a chance to get away by ourselves since the birth of our two children 3 years ago, so this was very special, being just the two of us.We used our Hilton points and hold the silver VIP membership. We checked in late around 8pm and orginally given a room on the 5th floor. The room was nice with the sink on the outside of the bathroom and a big king size bed. I had asked before I left the US what the availabilty was at the hotel and they has said full for the time I was staying there. I thought since it was a special trip I would go back down and see what I could do to get an upgrade. I just asked and explained by situation and viola! They upgraded us to the 7th floor, balcony room with the executive lounge priviledges! We moved all of our things to the new room and unpacked and checked out the fabulous view of the Eiffel tower from our balcony! We were in the last room on the 7th floor, however, I discovered that the shower head was broken. I called downstairs and after a promise to send someone up in a few minutes to fix it, we went to the executive lounge to check that out. After a couple of drinks, we went back to our room to find that the shower head was not fixed as of yet. Again I called downstairs and they informed me that the part has been ordered for quite sometime and still has not come in. They don't know when it will come in, probably at some point during our stay, but not in the next day or so. So again we were moved to another room, this time closer to the elevators. The room was exactally the same, except the further room had a much bigger safe. So again we packed and unpacked and moved. Finally we showered and changed and played under the sheets and then we went to bed by 2am! After all it was our first night in the city of love! How could we not?? The room was bigger than the one on the 5th floor and had a flat screen tv. Which did stop working one night, but was fixed the next morning. There are only 2 channels you get in English and alot in French and Arabic. I think we saw about 15 minutes of tv if that during our whole stay. There are games you can play on the tv as well, which my husband discovered one night and had a blast playing them while I had a nice long soak in the tub. The bathroom had the sink and standing shower along with a large bathtub all in one room, not separate like the one on the 5th floor. Maid service was good, though they did not speak any English. We had turn down service each night with two liitle boxes of chocolates on the pillows! Yummy! The shampoo and shower gel, is not too good, so you may want to bring your own. They do give you a wash clothes, shower cap, embry board, q-tips, shoe shine, and of course soap. You also get two large and fluffy bathrobes and slippers! The bed was comfortable with goose down comforter and 3 large fluffy pillows. The weather was in the low 70's and over-cast to sunny all of our days there and one if it were any hotter, I don't think the a/c would of been sufficent. I don't know if there was something wrong with our a/c but we had it on the whole time we were there and it barley felt cool. The weather was perfect and it only rained one day for 15 minutes while we were standing in line to the Saint Chappell. Of course the only day we left our umbrellas in our hotel room as well! Figures right? The hotel is very nice in the Art Deco theme and very clean. The closest metro Courcelles is 1 3-5 minute walk. You will need to change to any place you go, not a big deal unless you are under time restrains. The metro by the Arc de Triomphe Charles de Gaulle Etoile is more central and that one is a good 15 minute walk. We took the Air France bus from the airport (pay on the bus, via euros). You can save 16E by buying a roundtrip ticket. It took about 45 minutes to get to our stop by the Arc and then we had only two roll-on bags and a back pack so we walked to the hotel. Not to hard to find at all. Be sure to have a map with you at this time. It comes in handy to find the hotel. If you take the taxi it will cost a min. of 6E, plus if you have bags, not worth it. The bus begins the trips to the airport at 5:45am bythe Arc and runs every 15 minutes or so. We took it back to the airport as well. Very easy and cost effective. We found the staff at the hotel to be just okay. Not really going out of their way, but doing their jobs. We had no problems aside from the broken shower head and the tv. The concerige were always willing to help and most helpful. There are taxis at all times outside of the hotel so that's never a problem either. We did not eat at the hotel restraunts, but did look at the menus and they were very pricey! The bar was pretty busy a couple of nights. There were lots of business as well as leisure travelers the time we were there. But the hotel never felt crowed. There is a very high fee to use the internet at the hotel. We saw many internet cafes that were a lot cheaper around the city. There are two phone booths right outside the hotel which we used nightly to call home to check on the kids. Very handy as it is insainly expensive to use the hotel room phones! We were gone all day everyday from early in the morning to late at night except our last two days there. On those two days, we went to the Executive lounge in the early evenings and found it to be quite full. They did have the same food out for breakfast each day, but plenty of food to get you started. Dinnertime they did have different food the two nights we were there and for late night snacks, they had different things almost each night. Of course there was not a lot of choices, but a few finger sandwiches and the such. Not too bad. One night they had really good food and alot of it and I could of made that my dinner, had I not just eaten two hours before! They always had coke, orange juice, beer, water, champagne, wine, gin, vodka, rum and brandy availabe each day. Apples and bananas each day along with a nice fruit salad each morning. If you can get an upgrade, by all means do try! I heard if you can't get the upgrade, try to get the free breakfast, they usually give you that which is around 20E or so. The street across the metro station Courcelles, has many little shops and places to eat. We found a couple of fun places, Indiana a tex-mex restraunt that was always busy in the evenings and good food at good prices on Hoche street, about a 8 minute walk going towards the Arc. One of the best Cholcalatiers in also nearby, called La Maison du Chocolat on 225 rue du Faubourg St Honore, again only a 8 minute walk away. Nicholas is a grocery store and good deals on wines and beers which is across the street from the Courcelles metro stop. There is no shuttle that goes between this hotel and the Eiffel tower as some have indicated. Perhaps they only run it in the summer? I asked several employees there and none knew anything about this. Since we used the executive lounge for breakfast, after dinner snacks, we really saved a lot of money. We usually ate on the run, simply because of all the sites we wanted to take in, so we did not go to many of the recommended restraunts, but there are tons of places to eat so that shouldn't be a problem. Another benefit being the on 7th floor is that you get to use the spa whirlpool for free, otherwise there is a 25E charge. There is a sauna and a steam room. We only found time to use it on our very last day there, but enjoyed it emmensely as we were the only two in there! The water however in the jaccuzzi was barley warm, but we didn't let that stop us from having fun! You do not need to know much French at all to enjoy the city. I knew probably 30 phrases and I barely got to use them...85% people speak enough to answer your questions no matter where you are. Even those who do not speak any English, we found we could communicate with them without much effort as well. The metro are very easy to use, realiable, fast and cost effective. By the un carnate (10 tickets) or carte orange if you will be using the metro 3-4 times a day. We had a wonderful and romantic time while we were in Paris! If and when we go back someday I don't think I would stay here again, only becasue of the location. Yes, it is quite, but too much walking to get to the center of the city and all the major sites. We did enjoy our time at the hotel in our larger upgraded room and the executive lounge privileges made our stay just that much better!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel - but try to avoid the rooms to the street Stay on the executive floor in Dec 2005 was good value for the money given that I had made a reservation for a standard room over a week-end and was upgraded through a HHonors Gold card. When I came back in May 2006 for a business trip, I got a standard room with windows to the street which was quite noisy. Others might be less sensitive to French drivers roaring through the streets at 3 a.m. and people shouting there, but I could not get any sleep throughout the whole night.Frankly speaking, I had spent nights in a discount hotel on the Porte de Montreuil for 35 EUR per night which turned out more comfortable than here at the Hilton Arc de Triomphe. When I asked for another room with windows to the court yard for the following nights, I was given a room which was really fine and quiet.Another drawback is that the hotel is indeed situated relatively remote. As another traveller in this forum has pointed out correctly, Hilton Arc de Triomphe is a bit misleading as a name, in the sense that you will not even be able to see the Arc from the hotel. You rather have to have a 10 minutes walk to arrive there. The next metro station is officially Courcelles, but as far as the walking distances are concerned, it is almost arbitrage-free whether you walk to Charles de Gaulle Etoile on the Champs or to Courcelles - especially given the fact that you are immediately on the RER line when walking to CdG Etoile. 10 minutes walking distance to the next trou de mtro is already at the upper range of what one could expect in central Paris.To sum up, for the relative remoteness and the risk of getting a noisy room, I consider the hotel slightly overpriced. There are hotels of the same standard in this district which appear less remote and noisy and offer standard at a slighly more reasonable price (Sofitel among others).One final adivce for holders of Hilton HHonors Gold VIP cards: Although holders are normally granted complimentary access to the health club and fitness centers at the hotel, the card is not valid for free access to the hotel spa unless you reside on the executive floor.

<Author>dfwbob
<Content>what a great stay............ Well we just returned from our Paris trip and can't say enough about how well everything went.The Hilton was a pleasure. We had a room on the 7th floor with a balcony the size of my first apartment and arrived to find champagne from the Hilton in our room (I am only gold level).The bed and linens were very comfortable and the room was quiet!Each night at turndown the were different chocolates and the executive lounge on the 6th floor stayed open till 11pm. They offered breakfast each morning and wine ,drinks and snacks all day.The Coucelles metro stop is two blocks away and the Camps Elysee is a mere 10 minute walk the other direction.We purchased a Carte Orange for the metro which is good for unlimited use from Monday- Sunday (bring a small photo). The Hotel staff was very helpful with directions and restaurant reservations. A great place nearby was Le Bistro de Sommalier on Haussman. It was one of our best dining adventures of the week. We went with the Chefs Menu which consisted of 5 courses paired with wonderfull wines for 70 euros each.Another hotel suggestion was Boeuf Sur La Troit just a ten minute walk south.A great Paris bistro and open on Sundays when most other places were closed.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A little taste of luxury! My boyfriend and I stayed here for two nights, Sat 6th and Sun 7th May. From the moment we walked in we knew we would enjoy our stay. The decor throughout the entire hotel is beautiful - very grand. We used the separate HHonors check in desk, and as my boyfriend is a Hilton Diamond member, we were requested to go up to the Executive Lounge to check in. The Lounge staff are wonderful - nothing is too much trouble.We had been upgraded to a Executive room which was wonderful - bathrobes, slippers, complimentary water and chocolates each night. Again, the rooms, whilst on the dark side, are beautifully decorated, with nice toiletries. Massive, comfortable bed, large bath, small balcony overlooking a courtyard and a radio/CD player which was tuned in to a classical station and playing when we walked in! Nice touches.The Lounge provided us with a place to relax in the evening drinking complimentray champagne, and snacking on chips, pralines, nuts, olives, fruit, and hot snacks. I believe they had sandwiches and hot snacks throughout the day but we were exploring Paris and missed most of those! The Lounge is a nice place to meet and talk to others. We ate breakfast there the first morning, great service and nice food, but we thought the selection was smaller than the previous Hilton we stayed in. Still, cereals, pastries, coffee tea, hot items, fruits meats, cheeses and rolls, etc etc etc. The second morning we asked to eat downstairs in the main hotel restaurant, where the food selection is SO much better!! Try the lounge and the restaurant if you can.The staff happily stored our luggage on the last day, and again, they were all so polite and courteous. The Hotel is not in the centre of Paris, but Metro stop Courceles is a few minutes walk, or a ten minute walk to the Arc de Triomphe where the regional express trains (RER) stop.All in all, a fantastic stay, obviously made better by the upgrade to the Exec Floors. Hopefully we'll be going back!! Contact me with any questions!

<Author>name_screen
<Content>Excellent stay at Hilton Arc de Triomphe I stayed at the Hilton Arc de Triomphe for one week on business. The beds are very comfortable with down pillows. The rooms are large for Paris, and include an in-room safe, hair dryer, mini-bar, high-speed internet (fee). Concierge is very helpful finding restaurants if you would like recommendations. Breakfast is available as continental (19EUR) or full (30EUR), make sure you mention which breakfast you want. Hotel lobby is very art-deco and tends to be a bit smoke-filled. Purple Bar is fine for cocktails. Nearest metro is Courcelles, about 2 blocks away; a taxi to CDG airport is about 35-40EUR. Overall, this hotel is good for business travelers or tourists.

<Author>xmapjoen
<Content>Nice hotel, shame about the location Stayed in this art decoish hotel for a long weekend. Everything up to 4 star Hilton standards although the rooms on the compact side and for Paris exceptionally quiet.Although hotel was full room service was never longer than 15 minutes for breakfast. And to call it the Hilton Arc de Triomphe is taking liberties. The hotel does not have any views at all of the Arc (or of anything but the nearby offices) and is a good 10 minutes walk from the Arc.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous! We loved Hilton in the fall. Hello Paris-lovers,This is a hotel for you!My husband and I took a weekend get-away in a quite rainy and cold Paris, in October. And yet, it is one of the best weekend-experiences we've ever had. Hilton Arc de Triomphe is a splendid hotel and the atmosphere is outstanding. Paris is even better in the fall, than in the summer. We took a lazy stroll down a calm Champes Elysee, and walked down all the way, to the Louvre. We got there at 7 o'clock at night and wandered the place almost alone. Extraodinaire feeling, almost out of this world. It was us and the great artists, a friendly and completely stress-less experience. We were alone with Mona Lisa and couldn't help thinking about the Da Vinci Code... Afterwards, we took a taxi to a restaurant called Spice. A nice and cozy restaurant with a 100% Paris-feel to it. Quite cheap and very romantic.Enough about that and more about the hotel.We actually got a cheaper rate from their own website, so check it out. The hotel itself is more expensive than most hotels, but it's SO WORTH IT!The decor is suductive and very romantic, and the service is excellent. The lobby is like I would imagine Titanic's decor was.This is a hotel experience to remember, and we loved it.Breakfast is quite expensive, as they say, but very parisian and we recommend taking a long lunch beside the windows. Sip a cup of coffee, read a news paper and relax.The rooms are so very nice and actually quite ..sexy. I loved the dressing/bathroom. :))Don't forget to have a drink in the bar, when you feel for it. We had a late night-cap, and strongly recommend it.We will absolutely return again, for a nice get away.The hotel is located perfectly. Just off the beaten tourist track, and yet so very close to everything! We have been to quite some hotels and restaurants over the years, in Paris, including the most luxurious ones you can find, all the way down to the middle priced ones. Mark my words - this hotel is different from others, and it gives you a very nice experience.We hold it very high on our personal around the world-hotel list.Enjoy your stay, you will not regret checking in here.  
<Date>Mar 5, 2006

<Author>mparel
<Content>Perfect Hotel With Perfect Staff My husband and I just returned from a 3 night stay in this hotel. We rely on trip advisor for hotel reviews, so we thought we should add ours. From check-in to departure, everything was perfect. We were escorted to the executive level for an expresso while registering then escorted to the room. As in the brochure and on the hotel web site, the room had a balcony and a picture perfect view of the Eiffel Tower. It was ready for our 9:30 AM arrival, even though I had requested an early 10 AM check-in. As others have noted, this is a newer hotel (almost 2 years old, I think)and everything is still in excellent condition from the bedding to the baths. The rooms and baths really are like the pictures. Our plasma TV did indeed work just fine. The executive lounge is wonderful: Madame Catherine will even make dinner reservations for you. Refreshments and snacks (including beer, excellent wines and champagnes - complimentary) were served throughout the day starting with breakfast and constantly replenished. Dinner in the hotel restaurant was a very pleasant experience. The wait staff, especially Mademoiselle Cira, was excellent and the food was far superior to many of the restaurants having one of the coveted stars.My husband says I am too picky when it comes to hotels, and we have stayed in some of the best in the world (e.g., Lord Byron - Rome, Mauna Kea Resort- Hawaii, Peninsula - Hong Kong) but in all honesty, I have absolutly nothing but good things to say about this Hilton. We paid a discounted rate for our room (#777 on the top floor) yet experienced first class service. As long as the hotel maintains the service and ambiance that we experienced this time, we intend to stay here whenever we are in Paris.

<Author>TMM
<Content>You could do better, you could do worse... I feel a bit guilty about the review I have to give as the stay was a freebie after entering a competition on the UK Conde Nast Traveller website last December. The reception desk was great and very helpful and we were allowed to check into our room very early. This was a bonus as we did want a nap before going out. We were upgraded to a King deluxe suite which consisted on two bathrooms (only one with a bath), living room and a separate bedroom. The dcor of the suite and hotel is nice.Besides reception, service was virtually none existent. We called three times to have the plasma TV in our bedroom repaired as there was no reception. When the technician did show up he said very little except the TV was broken which we already knew. He offered us nothing and then my husband asked if the regular TV set in the living room could be moved to the bedroom. He swapped the TVs and we suspect whoever stays in the room next (room 424) will have to make a few calls if they wish to watch TV in the lounge area.The hallway leading to our room was constantly littered and quite a few stains on the carpets. When we arrived there were dirty drinking glasses in front of our door and when we left (two days later) the same glass was there. Kid you not. It wasn like they were concealed.Room service was appalling and way overpriced even by Paris standards. We ordered a cheese plate that came with two small pieces of cheese (mold and all) and a small bistro salad, a croque monsieur that was cold and bottle of Evian for 50 euros. Had the food been good food, no problem, but it wasn so we can give room service a good review.We also had access to the Executive Lounge. The food offerings were slim. It was okay for a drink before going out, but the EL was not worth the upgrade price. Again the service was non-existent and the lounge is pretty much self service.We have stayed in many hotels in Paris and this is not one we would rush back to. There are too many choices in Paris at the same rate level to choose from.

<Author>Isky
<Content>Loved it My husband and I stayed at this hotel for three nights in September and loved it. The king size bed was incredibly comfortable and the dark drapes and heavy lining under them kept the sun out....we woke up one day to a dark room and it was 1pm! Very romantic hotel with marble bathroom, great toilitries and four large towels, the size of beach towels. Breakfast was just okey...but very expensive - about 30 euros per person. I never made it to the spa because we were so close to the tourist sites and there was so much to do. The Arc de Triomph was a five minute walk, as was the metro station. The Hilton staff was wonderful at speaking English and very informative in helping us with a show at the Lido and providing huge hotel umbrellas for the days it rained. I would highly recommend this hotel and would stay their again. During our walks near the Arc de Triomph, we did not see any hotels that would compare to this Hilton.

<Author>DSKMD
<Content>Not great for families We spent 3 nights (July 17-19) at this Hilton after reviewing feedback on this site regarding the Hilton Arc de Triomphe. As a family of five, I was concerned with finding decent sized rooms and beds. My initial night, I kept my reservation for 2 rooms, both with 2 queen sized beds, but since our flight from Italy came in late in the afternoon, they could not accomodate our request for 2 connecting rooms. Also, they would not upgrade like many of the HHonors members who seem to write on this site for this hotel. They gave us rooms on the 3rd floor facing the street. If you have young children, mine were 3, 8, and 11, you might be able to squeeze into one room. The 2 separate rooms were overkill and also very expensive. The Hilton website allows only 4 per room, but it is up to you whether you'd rather spend it on sleeping or out on the town.I picked this Hilton as it seemed close to the Air France shuttle dropoff at the Arc de Triomphe. This hotel is too far to comfortably walk to the hotel with all your luggage. Our taxi ride albeit a few long blocks cost us 11 Euros due to added costs of each bag stored in the trunk. I found out that there is a courtesy van that makes stops at the Arc from the hotel starting at 10:15 am on the hour, but only accomodates 8 passangers and you have to ride it to the Hilton Eiffel tower before going back to the Hilton, another 45 minutes total.Breakfast was included in our package, constituting various ethnicities, but the same each day. Eggs were unusually runny! We stayed at the Hilton Charles de Gaulle when we first arrived in Europe and for half the price and the same Hilton service and food, I enjoyed this much better given it's 5 minute free shuttle right from the airport, walking distance to trains into the city and access to the Air France shuttle right into town. Great for families just arriving as we could put our children to bed immediately after arriving to get them acclimated without adding extra travel.Everyone is right, the Hilton Arc de Triomphe is not convenient to many nice eateries nor stores although about 2 long blocks to the metro and down rue de Berri toward the Champs Elysee.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Hilton! I stayed 3 nights in Paris at the Hilton and loved it! I spent a lot of time reading reviews of hotels in Paris, and finally selcted this hotel. I wasn't thrilled that I would have to spend as much as we did, but July in Paris in a comfortable hotel with great service has its price. I was not disappointed!At first I was worried about how far I would be from the major attractions, but it wasn't too bad after all. Most of the time we walked 2 minutes to and from the Metro when we went exploring. The Arc de Triomphe was just 7-10 minutes walk from the hotel, so one night we took a stroll to see the Arc at night. We were also informed that the hotel had a shuttle bus that went between the Arc de Triomphe and the hotel every hour on the hour (except lunchtime) from morning until about 6 pm. The weather was great so we never used it.The service was fantastic. When we checked in I asked for a room with a decent view. The young lady recommended the patio as being the nicest view. No fantastic view of the city, but it was pleasant enough. The staff was there to assist with restaurant suggestions, train reservations, just about anything.Our room was clean and smelled fresh. Towels and sheets were sparkling white. Turn down service was an unexpected bonus. Typically we returned to the hotel before dinner to shower and change. Every evening when we returned from dinner, our room had been freshned up (again) - the bed was straightened, and we even got fresh towels (again). The room wasn't huge, but a comfortable size for a couple. We asked for, and got a king-sized bed in a non-smoking room.I wanted a hotel that I would look forward to returning to every evening, and the Hilton fit the bill. Every evening before going to bed, we stopped in the Purple Bar to relax, have a drink and talk about the day's adventure. A great setting to end the day.The Hilton isn't cheap, but for 3 days we spoiled ourselves in Paris and had a lovely time. I would not hesitate to return to the Hilton on my next visit to Paris.

The bathroom has a separate bath tub and shower. I travelled alone hence the room was perfectly sized, for two persons it would be on the small size.Service was very friendly and helpful. Restaurant offers good food, but be aware of very high beer prices (EUR 16 for a pint of lager in the restaurant!)..Location of the hotel is in a business district, but then again it is only a 10 min. walk to Etoile.Alltogether I would recommend this hotel mainly to business travellers.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This Is Not a Great Hotel Just came back from a 5 night stay on my honeymoon. We had stayed the previous 6 nights in beautiful hotels in Rome and Nice and we're completely thrown off by our stay at the Hilton Arc. Let's face it folks, read the rest of the reviews and you'll find that everyone is either a HH Gold Member (oooooooh) or stayed in Executive class. If you don't have that sought after Gold Card and are just looking for a nice hotel in Paris.....this is not the one for you!. It is completely out of the way (15 minute walk to any signs of life). There is nothing open past 7:00 pm around the hotel. It is quiet because it is in the middle of a business area. The 3 square pillows you get are full of sand, and after waking up with a broken back, I asked the front desk if they could move us to a room with a better bed. Instead, they sent 2 guys to our room to place a big board under the mattress. There are far better hotels, in far better locations, for a far better value!

<Author>jdvmd
<Content>Wonderful stay at the Hilton We had a wonderful stay at the Hilton. Great location, close to the Courcelles metro (about a five-minute walk) and wonderful little neighborhood that include a small grocery store, wine store (Nicholas), cheese and sorbet shop etc. Just around the corner of the hotel and down the street a few steps, you will see the Arc de Triumphe and the Champs Elysses. When I return to Paris, I would stay here again in a second. This is a new hotel having opened last year. I don't know why someone would say it is showing its age. Beautiful condition and very, very clean. The valet and bellstaff were wonderful as were the the concierge, Purple bar and front desk staff. The room we had was 250 Euros a night for two double beds. (We are a family of four). Wonderful duvet. Would have liked to have had more pillows but I never bothered to ask for them. I am Hilton Honors but never received anything including a paper. Our traveling companions received welcome macaroons and a note from the manager but they were booked in a family suite which was 400 Euros a night.

<Content>Impressed I stayed for 3 nights for around Eur250 a night, not quite a steal as some other travellers here. Yes, location is not too central, but I enjoy the fact that the neighbourhood is quiet. Furthermore, its not that bad. The nearest subway is Courcelles station, and its a 5 min walk. The pricing turns out to be reasonable although I thought everything in Paris tends to be pricey. Overall, the room is nice. I had a twin, which is great in terms of size. General service level is good and staff are courteous. Would stay there again if I visit Paris again.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Terrific stay Stayed here end of June. Agree with previous posts regarding location. Although close to the Champs d'Elysee, it is a bit off the beaten track. It is located in a neighbourhood of embassies and banks. Very little in the immediate vicinity. This does allow for a quiet sleep. Found a great restaurant on my last day. Head straight out the front door, down Blvd Lisbon (two minute walk) to Place Rio de Janero. Here you will find Restaurant Valois with its red awning. Traditional bistro fare (steak tartare, moules, escargots). Super busy at lunch with bankers etc.. dead at night as is the rest of the neighbourhood. Do stop at Parc Monceau which is right by the hotel. A truly beautiful oasis and a great spot to people watch...Back to the hotel: Comfortable, clean air conditioned rooms (the AC is weak especially when used en masse during a heat wave). Executive lounge very pleasant. Spa was lovely after a day of walking. Outdoor terrace restaurant also lovely. Service throughout stay fantastic. I would definitely return, but I would price shop. I stayed for 199 euros which I felt was a steal. Side note: since my last visit to Paris I found taxi service to be appalling. Several drivers had just begun their careers. Speak to them before you hop in if you can. If they don't know Paris, wait for another driver.

<Content>Fantastic Hotel Just got back from the Hilton Arc de Triomphe and wanted everyone to know what a great hotel it is. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>best hotel staff My husband and I and our two teenagers stayed at the Hilton Arc de Triomphe for a three-night weekend during a family vacation. We had a family guest room, which included two bedrooms and two bathrooms. The rooms were comfortable and well-appointed. The Weekend in Style rate included an extensive and excellent buffet breakfast, with a variety of fresh fruit (cantelope, watermelon, pineapple, mixed fruit, oranges, apples, bananas), pancakes, sausage, eggs, hash browns, assorted delicous pastries and breads, cheeses, meats, cereals, yogurts, a variety of juices, and other items. The hotel is lovely, with art deco styling throughout. We found the location to be convenient to the Champs-lyses and pretty much every place that we wanted to go. It's a relatively quiet area, about a five minute walk to the Champs-lyses. We enjoy walking and also walked to the Louvre, the Opera Garnier (worth visiting, especially if you're a Phantom fan), Muse d'Orsay, and Notre Dame Cathedral. The latter may be further than many people would want to walk, but it was a good excuse to walk along the Seine.Even though this was not a business trip, we used the business center in the evening - our son kept in touch with friends on the internet and we used the computer to transfer photos from a digital camera to an iPod.The best thing about this hotel was the staff. Every individual that we encountered in this hotel was completely professional and personally welcoming at the same time. I was continually under the impression that it was the priority of each employee to ensure that our stay at the Hilton was the best possible experience. It is common to hear that the French do not like Americans and may not always treat them well, but our experience at this hotel was just the opposite. We have stayed in hotels in Germany, Italy, Austria, the United Kingdom, Canada, and all over the U.S. We've had many good experiences, but the staff of this Hilton were the best we have ever enountered. We would definitely return to this hotel.  
<Date>Apr 7, 2005

<Author>worldtraveler089
<Content>Very nice-only a few minor problems First of all I want to say that being an avid traveler I am tough when it comes to reviews. The hotel must be truly extraordinary with no problems to get an excellent rating. I stayed at this property for one night on March 26th. Upon arrival, I was immediately escorted to the executive lounge for check-in. Dissappointingly, there were no available rooms for check-in. I couldn't really complain because it was early (around 10am) Being a diamond member, I asked for an upgrade to a suite. I was told however there would be a 200 euro charge to upgrade and that being a diamond member meant an executive plus room with views of the eiffel tower and arc was the best they could do. I was ok with this and actually content with the idea of of having a view. I was told the room would be ready around 3pm I returned around 6pm and was instead given a deluxe king suite on the 2nd floor, with no view. I was very happy given that my earlier request was honored. Come to find out it was only because the hotel was oversold.What can I say, the suite was beautiful. Beautiful greenish black marble in the bathroom. Separate shower and tub. An abundance of bath amenities. Plush down comforters and pillows. There was also a bottle of red wine and pastries on the coffee table in the living room. It was truly spectacular.Now for problem #1. It was unusually warm that day in Paris and I noticed the air conditioning only worked in the living room, so I cracked the window open in the bedroom hoping I would get some air flow. Well that didn't happen. At around midnight I woke up in a sweat. It must of been around 80 in there. I called the front desk to complain and at first the receptionist was a bit perplexed that I was asking for air conditioning in March, but I explained to her that it was stifiling and she agreed to send maintenance. I am sure she probably thought I was an ugly american to ask for AC in March, but who cares I was hot!! The maintenance guy came up and after about 40 minutes he finally fixed it and I was able to sleep.The next morning the breakfast was great. There was plenty of food, no lines, and prompt service.All in all it was a nice hotel. The location is not too great, kind of far from the nightlife of Paris, but close if you like shopping on the Champs Elysees.I would stay here again, but only if I could use hilton points.

<Author>snooky
<Content>Very Good service. Staff Excellent. The Hilton Arc De Triomphe is about a 4 - 8 minute walk from that very monument. We were met at the door by a fully rigged out doorman, who spotted us walking up from the Metro... he took our bags and asked us our name.. We told him, and he nodded and took our name out from under his cap!!.. he then said, follow me.....we had a check-in on floor 6 and stayed on 7 which is the executive floor. This is because we are Hilton Gold card members and meant we also had free tea/coffee, cakes etc throughout the day in the executive lounge - Breakfast is served in there as well. Very good value. Sadly, even though we had been given free access to the Spa at the hotel, our daughter aged 9 wasn't allowed in, as you had to be over 18 to enter. This meant we didn't go at all, because she was quite upset she wasn't allowed in and had been looking forward to using the Jacuzzi etc and we didn't want to rub salt into the wound.  The view from our room at night was nice....Eiffel Tower.. and it sparkled on the hour for about 10 minutes. The room wasn't big, but adequate (two doubles), nicely decorated though you couldn't open the doors under the television to get to the drawers, which was a bit silly, as it got jammed into the bed. A little box of chocolates and fruit drinks were complementary.  We had a few problems with the TV, but they were sorted. A big thanks to Catherine on executive staff who was around to help us and give a friendly smile at all times. We used the business services which were also fine.  The nearest metro stop is Courcelles. I'd probably try the Hilton Paris next time as this was nearer the 'bright lights' of the Seine and Eiffel tower, but I would also stay at this hotel again. The nightly charge at this time of year for us was 230 euros.  May I really recommend on walking up the road to see the Arc De Triomphe stopping off at a small cafe called Midor which you will find at 236 rue Fbg St Honor (turn left out of hotel, next left up Avenue Hoche, then left again into Rue Fbg St Honore.. a few buildings down on the left hand side of the road) They have superb snack food. I had a quiche with potato/mushroom and spicy sausage which was out of this world, and the pizza and croque monsieur was sooooo tasty. A Really good little snack bar and first introduction to French food.

<Author>mark4
<Content>superb business hotel December 2004: I have just returned from a stay in this excellent hotel. Because of my HH gold status I was upgraded to the Executive floor without even having to request it - very unusual for the Hilton Group. This really is a top quality hotel and I am surprised they opted to call it a Hilton rather than Hiltons flagship group, Conrad. The hotel is appointed to a very high specification in attractive art deco style, this comprehensive refit still seems very new. The rooms are beautifully appointed, very quiet and feature superb beds and bed linen. All the staff were friendly and helpful. I would happily stay there again if I wished to stay in this location. The location is in fact the only issue. As a business location it is ideal. As a tourist location less so, it is rather hardwork to get around Paris requiring a change of Metro lines. There seems to be a desperate shortage of taxis late at night in Paris, making this location hard to get to once the metro has closed.
